< text>
My husband and I randomly chose to live at Camden Sierra from an online search from our previous duty station. It was one of the BEST decisions we have ever made. We lived at Camden Sierra for 2 years and were happy with our living experience. Assigned parking spots near apartment, quick and responsive maintenance staff, regularly maintained pool and outdoor grilling area, and interior of the apartments was nicely updated and maintained. We had friendly neighbors and enjoyed living in the Camden Sierra community. Yes, rent was raised each time our lease was up for renewal, but that is very typical for Southern California. There are many pet owners in the complex, so it was common to see droppings around the premises, but maintenance was typically quick to clean up (and pet owners should really be cleaning up after their own dogs). Great location of apartments, nice view, not on a busy road, schools nearby, easy commute to work. Lots of military personnel within the community. Highly recommend.< /text>

<Review>I’ve been going here on and off for about four years, and have been worked up to coming nearly every day since I got my license last year. Most of my workout is done on the elliptical and rowing machines, but there are weights I can use if I want to do a bit of strength training. I have the black card membership, so I always use the massage chairs or beds afterwards (I don’t use the tanning beds due to the potential for skin damage and premature aging) They don’t have some of the amenities you might find at Kennedy, such as a pool or a steam room, but that’s obviously because it’s so much more affordable. However it is extremely annoying when no one is manning the front desk and you want to use the massage chairs or beds etc or want to buy something and you have to go like find someone in the back which is hard when you have anxiety. There should always be one person at the front desk to help people with stuff like that in my opinion, and if they don’t want to hire more staff switch to automated system that allows people to check in on their own. Also, the wifi is often spotty and doesn’t work when there’s a lot of people. <name>Daniel George< /name>< Review>
So far, I like it a lot.  It would be nice if they had longer weekend hours.  Early Saturday morning is my favorite workout time.  I have a black card membership, and their hydrotherapy massage tables are wonderful after a workout.  Nice variety of machines, kept clean, and a large number of them too; so, you don't need to wait for a machine.  More weight machines would be nice.  I also wish the trainer was there more often, though it's nice that you get unlimited training with membership.  Friendly, helpful staff, but even better if more were working at the same time.  I love their no lunk rules!  I am an overweight man trying to improve my fitness and health, and I feel comfortable, welcome, and not judged when I work out there. Kimberly Ferdinand<//username>
<time>1610217895334<//time><Rating>1<//Rating>< review>
Ok! I went to this Trader Joe's for the first time. I was in my nursing apparel and had my badge in hand. I simply wanted to stop by and grab a few items after working a long depressing shift. I presented my badge to the gentleman at the door and he tells me that they are no longer allowing essential workers to enter the store and we are to wait as well. Now I normally shop at the Trader Joe's in Fremont but I relocated to Oakland. Now Healthcare workers don't ask for much and I literally ook that as a Slap in the face. I know that ever RN and physician is incredibly pressed for time because we are all working extremely long, exhausting, and chaotic hours. Now you mean to tell me when we get off we have to stand in line 20 - 30 min. before we can go into a store to make some much needed grocery. I declare this was the 1st and last time that I will ever shop at this Trader Joe's. If I was not so tired and depressed about all the patients that I see dying from CVD everyday, I would have left this store without shopping at all. Plus I just wanted to grab a few things to take to work so that I could have something to eat. This World Truly Have Issues especially when you take a simple gesture and discard during such chaotic times!!!</review>

Favorite place to go for groceries!

Parking: Shares a parking lot with the other stores at the Alameda Shore Center.

Prices: It's not a dollar store, but I think they are pretty decent and worth it. It's definitely cheaper than Whole Foods if that helps you get a better idea of the prices they offer.

The food: Many options. They have organic, gluten free, and vegan options too.

Tip: Please bring a bag to put your groceries in or you will be paying for a grocery bag. California laws, and a good one because we care about the environment.

Will I go again: Yes< /Review>

< Text>
OMG, this is my local Trader Joe's, which I visit on average five times a week, and somehow I've never reviewed it? How's that possible? Argh!

Trader Joe's store #109 is located in the middle of the South Shore Shopping Center. There's hundreds of parking spots immediately out front. Conveniently located near the corner of Park Street and Otis Drive, this is the to-go spot for dozens of staples, some keto-friendly foods (including grilled artichoke hearts, cheeses, eggs, hamburger, pork tenderloin, turkey breast, and sopressata salami), and the many TJ-specific offerings (including truffle pâte, many really good coffee beans, and seasonal surprises like unsweetened bakers chocolate, cakes and cookies, and mystery bags).

The non-food items, like greeting cards, plants and flowers, and a wide selection of beer, wine, and hard liquors round out any shopping trip.

The staff are absolutely wonderful, know their stock and where they may be found, and are always ready to help you find a TJ treasure. I'm very proud of my local store and hope you come on over to share in the joy.<//Text>

<UserId.>115715200304364963368</UserId.>< name>
Lea S</name>
<Date>1494014739732<//Date><Rate>4</Rate>< text>
Our go-to store. We come here weekly, because they have a good selection of veggies, fruits, meats, cheeses, snacks, beers and wines. Not to mention the staff is really friendly and the store is well kept (compared to Safeway next door where things are all over the place).

It's not pricey and it's convenient since you have a big parking place and many other stores around (in case you can't get everything here). Sometimes they don't have certain things cause they are changing the labels or getting in something new from someone else, but if you ask they might find something in the back or just tell you the date when they're getting it back on their shelves.

The only downside is that perishable things tend to go bad before their expiration date (salads and fruit I'm looking at you) and we do put them in the fridge and take all the necessary precautions.

The lines are not too long because the staff makes sure there's a sufficient number of check-outs open (again compared to Safeway where you have two registers and 20 people). But if you want to avoid the place being too crowded come in right after they open.

I don't care much for the samples they have, but I was told they are also good.

Would highly recommend you to come here instead of going into Safeway next door.</text>

<Text>i love trader joes, especially if i can manage to go at the lower traffic times. (weekday mornings, especially Wednesday.)

they do a lot of private label stuff, but it is uniformly high quality and lower prices than the equivalent merchandise at safeway or whole foods. the selection is pretty reasonable, but they do not tend to have a lot of specialty products. for example, they have white, crimini, and portabella mushrooms, but no shiitakes.

the other thing they do is stock a smattering of intriguing products, often on a seasonal basis. examples include halumi cheese, Thai chili spiced almonds, and chocolate-covered ginger.< /Text>< pics>
